The Language of Magick

Natively known as: ˈmædʒɪ /ˈmædʒɪ/

...and he stood holding his hat and turned his wet face to the wind...
klui kīks ˈētar ˈroar kʷār woen klui ˈfāar kʷār ū ˈdedmi trō peurs
Pronunciation: /klui kiːks ˈeːtar ˈroar kʷaːr woen klui ˈfaːar kʷaːr uː ˈdedmi troː peurs/
Magick word order: and he stood holding hat his and turned his face wet to the wind
Note: Translator does not automatically do word order and only finds exact matches in your dictionary (will not find plurals, past-tense, etc.) However, all available affixes in the language may be used. Making the translator smarter is a work in progress.

Translation:

fā

/faː/

Other translations:

Affixes in this language:

ACT.OF | ADVERB | AUG | DIM | DOER | HAVING.QUALITY.OF | LIKELY.TO | NOUN.PLURAL.DEF | NOUN.PLURAL.INDEF | NOUN.SING.DEF | NOUN.SING.INDEF | PLACE.OF | PRODUCT.OF | QUALITY.OF.BEING | RELATING.TO | RESULT.OF.DOING | TO.CREATE | TO.MAKE | VERB.FUT.1PLURAL | VERB.FUT.1SING | VERB.FUT.2PLURAL | VERB.FUT.2SING | VERB.FUT.3PLURAL | VERB.FUT.3SINGF | VERB.FUT.3SINGM | VERB.IMPERF | VERB.PAST.1PLURAL | VERB.PAST.1SING | VERB.PAST.2PLURAL | VERB.PAST.2SING | VERB.PAST.3PLURAL | VERB.PAST.3SINGF | VERB.PAST.3SINGM | VERB.PERF | VERB.PRES.1PLURAL | VERB.PRES.1SING | VERB.PRES.2PLURAL | VERB.PRES.2SING | VERB.PRES.3PLURAL | VERB.PRES.3SINGF | VERB.PRES.3SINGM | nf | nm | v

Syllable structure: Custom defined
Stress pattern: Penultimate — stress is on the second last syllable
Word initial consonants: b, br, d, f, fl, fr, g, gl, gr, h, k, kl, kr, kʷ, l, m, n, p, pl, pr, r, s, sk, sp, st, t, tr, w
Mid-word consonants: b, bl, br, bs, bt, d, dd, dkʷ, dm, dw, f, ff, g, gg, gm, gn, gr, h, k, kk, kkʷ, kr, ks, ksk, ksp, kspl, kssp, kst, kstr, kt, kʷ, l, lg, lk, ll, ln, lp, ls, lt, ltr, lw, m, mb, mkʷ, mm, mn, mp, mpl, mpr, mw, n, nd, nf, nfl, nfr, ng, ngr, nk, nkl, nkr, nkʷ, nl, nn, ns, nskr, nsp, nst, nstr, nt, ntr, nw, p, pl, pp, ppl, ppr, pr, ps, pt, r, rb, rd, rf, rg, rk, rkʷ, rm, rn, rp, rr, rs, rsp, rt, rw, s, sd, sk, skʷ, sm, sp, ss, st, stkʷ, str, t, tkʷ, tr, ts, tt, ttr, w
Word final consonants: b, d, k, ks, l, m, n, nk, ns, nt, ps, r, rs, s, st, t
Phonological changes (in order of application):

  • i → e / _(C)e
  • b → v / V_V
  • s → ʤ / {i,u}_V
  • a → ɛ / {t,n}_#
  • k → Ø / _#

Spelling rules:

PronunciationSpelling
ː macron over vowel

Grammar

Main word order: Subject-Verb-Object-Oblique. "Mary opened the door with a key" turns into Mary opened the door with a key.
Adjective order: Adjectives are positioned after the noun.
Adposition: prepositions

Nouns

Singular Plural
Definite No affix
ˈmuplin /ˈmuplin/
the dog		 Suffix -e
muˈplene /muˈplene/
the dogs
Indefinite If ends with vowel: Suffix -t
Else: Suffix -uːt
muˈplinūt /muˈplinuːt/
a dog		 Suffix -i
muˈplini /muˈplini/
some dogs


Articles

Magick encodes definite article ‘the’, and indefinite article ‘a’ in noun affixes. See Noun section.

Pronouns

1st singular ku /ku/
I, me, mine
2nd singular hei /hei/
you, yours
3rd singular masc kīks /kiːks/
he, him, his
3rd singular fem i /i/
she, her, hers
1st plural tiun /tiun/
we, us, ours
2nd plural bre /bre/
you (all), yours
3rd plural skaun /skaun/
they, them, theirs

Imperfective aspect

The ‘imperfective’ aspect refers to ongoing actions, such as I am studying and habitual actions, such as I study (every night).
Magick uses an affix for imperfective:

Imperfective If ends with vowel: Suffix -smoe
Else: Suffix -uːsmoe
nīˌnīaˈrūsmoe /niːˌniːaˈruːsmoe/
is studying


Perfect aspect

The perfect aspect in English is exemplified in ‘I have read this book’, which expresses an event that took place before the time spoken but which has an effect on or is in some way still relevant to the present.
Magick uses an affix for the perfect aspect:

Perfect If ends with vowel: Suffix -st
Else: Suffix -eːst
ˌnīnīˈarēst /ˌniːniːˈareːst/


Numbers

Magick has a base-10 number system:

1 - grin
2 - su
3 - skei
4 - pū
5 - lē
6 - kin
7 - brī
8 - poe
9 - ˈpriurto
10 - prins
11 - prinsgrin “ten-one”
100 - grin ˈmilki “one hundred”
101 - grin ˈmilki grin “one hundred one”
200 - su ˈmilki
1000 - grin os “one thousand”

Derivational morphology

Adjective → adverb = Prefix hei-
Adjective → noun (the quality of being [adj]) = If starts with vowel: Prefix ark-
Else: Prefix arko-
Adjective → verb (to make something [adj]) = If starts with vowel: Prefix fr-
Else: Prefix frae-
Noun → adjective (having the quality of [noun]) = Prefix daː-
Noun → adjective relating to noun (e.g. economy → economic) = Prefix o-
Noun → verb (to create [noun]) = Prefix e-
Verb → adjective (result of doing [verb]) = If starts with vowel: Prefix oːnd-
Else: Prefix oːndaː-
Verb → adjective (likely to do [verb]) = If starts with vowel: Prefix on-
Else: Prefix oniː-
Verb → noun (the act of [verb]) = If starts with vowel: Prefix k-
Else: Prefix ku-
Verb → noun that verb physically produces (e.g. build → building) = Prefix kaː-
One who [verb]s (e.g. paint → painter) = Prefix riː-
Place of (e.g. wine → winery) = If starts with vowel: Prefix s-
Else: Prefix sa-
Diminutive = If starts with vowel: Prefix t-
Else: Prefix tiu-
Augmentative = If starts with vowel: Prefix p-
Else: Prefix poː-
